<pr_description>
Optimizer confluence produces assertion failure in OptStackOps / Opt_a_tossub
**Compiler and OS**
Current cc65 head with MSYS / MINGW64_NT-10.0-19045 3.6.6-2369286a.x86_64 (but I do not believe OS or build system matters).

**Describe the bug**
Certain expressions involving arithmetic with a compare operator (>=) trigger an invariant `CHECK()` in `Opt_a_tossub()` when code is optimized. Please see minimal failing test below. First discovered in the [bug2395.c expansion](https://github.com/avolkov76/cc65/blob/anv-bug-2461/test/val/bug2395.c).

**To Reproduce**
The minimal failing test is:
```C
/* bug #2946: Incomplete, non-removable Rhs asserts in OptStackOps */

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

unsigned char a, b = 0;
unsigned char c = 10;
unsigned char d = 1;

int main(void) {
    /* 'if' needed to produce a label below, moved by OptJumpTarget3  */
    if (b != 0) {
        /* Operation not important; it only affects the removal of one LDX #$00 */
        b = 0;
    }

    /* d >= 0 is const, A/X=1 (Warning: Result of comparison is always true) */
    a = c - (d >= 0);

    return !(a == 9);
}
```

    35	
    36	#include <stdlib.h>
    37	
    38	/* common */
    39	#include "chartype.h"
    40	
    41	/* cc65 */
    42	#include "codeent.h"
    43	#include "codeinfo.h"
    44	#include "codeoptutil.h"
    45	#include "coptstop.h"
    46	#include "error.h"
    47	
    48	
    49	
    50	/*****************************************************************************/
    51	/*                                   Data                                    */
    52	/*****************************************************************************/
    53	
    54	
    55	
    56	/* Flags for the functions */
    57	typedef enum {
    58	    OP_NONE              = 0x00,         /* Nothing special */
    59	    OP_A_KNOWN           = 0x01,         /* Value of A must be known */
    60	    OP_X_ZERO            = 0x02,         /* X must be zero */
    61	    OP_LHS_LOAD          = 0x04,         /* Must have load insns for LHS */
    62	    OP_LHS_SAME_BY_OP    = 0x08,         /* Load result of LHS must be the same if relocated to op */
    63	    OP_LHS_LOAD_DIRECT   = 0x0C,         /* Must have direct load insn for LHS */
    64	    OP_RHS_LOAD          = 0x10,         /* Must have load insns for RHS */
    65	    OP_RHS_SAME_BY_OP    = 0x20,         /* Load result of RHS must be the same if relocated to op */
    66	    OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT   = 0x30,         /* Must have direct load insn for RHS */
    67	    OP_AX_INTERCHANGE    = 0x40,         /* Preconditions of A/X may be interchanged */
    68	    OP_LR_INTERCHANGE    = 0x80,         /* Preconditions of LHS/RHS may be interchanged */
    69	    OP_LHS_SAME_BY_PUSH  = 0x0100,       /* LHS must load the same content if relocated to push */
    70	    OP_RHS_SAME_BY_PUSH  = 0x0200,       /* RHS must load the same content if relocated to push */
    71	    OP_LHS_SAME_BY_RHS   = 0x0400,       /* LHS must load the same content if relocated to RHS */
    72	    OP_RHS_SAME_BY_LHS   = 0x0800,       /* RHS must load the same content if relocated to LHS */
    73	    OP_LHS_REMOVE        = 0x1000,       /* LHS must be removable or RHS may use ZP store/load */
    74	    OP_LHS_REMOVE_DIRECT = 0x3000,       /* LHS must be directly removable */
    75	    OP_RHS_REMOVE        = 0x4000,       /* RHS must be removable or LHS may use ZP store/load */
    76	    OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT = 0xC000,       /* RHS must be directly removable */
    77	} OP_FLAGS;
    78	
    79	/* Structure that describes an optimizer subfunction for a specific op */
    80	typedef unsigned (*OptFunc) (StackOpData* D);
    81	typedef struct OptFuncDesc OptFuncDesc;
    82	struct OptFuncDesc {
    83	    const char*         Name;           /* Name of the replaced runtime function */
    84	    OptFunc             Func;           /* Function pointer */
    85	    unsigned            UnusedRegs;     /* Regs that must not be used later */
    86	    OP_FLAGS            Flags;          /* Flags */
    87	};
    88	
    89	
    90	
    91	/*****************************************************************************/
    92	/*                                  Helpers                                  */
    93	/*****************************************************************************/
    94	
    95	
    96	
    97	static int SameRegAValue (StackOpData* D)
    98	/* Check if Rhs Reg A == Lhs Reg A */
    99	{
   100	    RegInfo* LRI = GetLastChangedRegInfo (D, &D->Lhs.A);
   101	    RegInfo* RRI = GetLastChangedRegInfo (D, &D->Rhs.A);
   102	
   103	    /* RHS can have a -1 ChgIndex only if it is carried over from LHS */
   104	    if (RRI == 0                                    ||
   105	        (D->Rhs.A.ChgIndex >= 0         &&
   106	         D->Rhs.A.ChgIndex == D->Lhs.A.ChgIndex)    ||
   107	        (LRI != 0                       &&
   108	         RegValIsKnown (LRI->Out.RegA)  &&
   109	         RegValIsKnown (RRI->Out.RegA)  &&
   110	         (LRI->Out.RegA & 0xFF) == (RRI->Out.RegA & 0xFF))) {
   111	
   112	        return 1;
   113	    }
   114	
   115	    return 0;
   116	
   117	}
   118	
   119	
   120	
   121	static int SameRegXValue (StackOpData* D)
   122	/* Check if Rhs Reg X == Lhs Reg X */
   123	{
   124	    RegInfo* LRI = GetLastChangedRegInfo (D, &D->Lhs.X);
   125	    RegInfo* RRI = GetLastChangedRegInfo (D, &D->Rhs.X);
   126	
   127	    if (RRI == 0                                    ||
   128	        (D->Rhs.X.ChgIndex >= 0         &&
   129	         D->Rhs.X.ChgIndex == D->Lhs.X.ChgIndex)    ||
   130	        (LRI != 0                       &&
   131	         RegValIsKnown (LRI->Out.RegX)  &&
   132	         RegValIsKnown (RRI->Out.RegX)  &&
   133	         (LRI->Out.RegX & 0xFF) == (RRI->Out.RegX & 0xFF))) {
   134	
   135	        return 1;
   136	    }
   137	
   138	    return 0;
   139	
   140	}
   141	
   142	
   143	
   144	/*****************************************************************************/
   145	/*                       Actual optimization functions                       */
   146	/*****************************************************************************/
   147	
   148	
   149	
   150	static unsigned Opt_toseqax_tosneax (StackOpData* D, const char* BoolTransformer)
   151	/* Optimize the toseqax and tosneax sequences. */
   152	{
   153	    CodeEntry*  X;
   154	    CodeLabel* L;
   155	
   156	    /* Create a call to the boolean transformer function and a label for this
   157	    ** insn. This is needed for all variants. Other insns are inserted *before*
   158	    ** the call.
   159	    */
   160	    X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_JSR, AM65_ABS, BoolTransformer, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   161	    InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex + 1);
   162	    L = CS_GenLabel (D->Code, X);
   163	
   164	    /* If the lhs is direct (but not stack relative), encode compares with lhs
   165	    ** effectively reverting the order (which doesn't matter for ==).
   166	    */
   167	    if ((D->Lhs.A.Flags & (LI_DIRECT | LI_RELOAD_Y)) == LI_DIRECT &&
   168	        (D->Lhs.X.Flags & (LI_DIRECT | LI_RELOAD_Y)) == LI_DIRECT) {
   169	
   170	        CodeEntry* LoadX = D->Lhs.X.LoadEntry;
   171	        CodeEntry* LoadA = D->Lhs.A.LoadEntry;
   172	
   173	        D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;
   174	
   175	        /* cpx */
   176	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_CPX, LoadX->AM, LoadX->Arg, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   177	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   178	
   179	        /* bne L */
   180	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_BNE, AM65_BRA, L->Name, L, D->OpEntry->LI);
   181	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   182	
   183	        /* cmp */
   184	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_CMP, LoadA->AM, LoadA->Arg, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   185	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   186	
   187	        /* Lhs load entries can be removed if not used later */
   188	        D->Lhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
   189	        D->Lhs.A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
   190	
   191	    } else if ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & (LI_DIRECT | LI_RELOAD_Y)) == LI_DIRECT &&
   192	               (D->Rhs.X.Flags & (LI_DIRECT | LI_RELOAD_Y)) == LI_DIRECT &&
   193	               D->RhsMultiChg == 0) {
   194	
   195	        CodeEntry* LoadX = D->Rhs.X.LoadEntry;
   196	        CodeEntry* LoadA = D->Rhs.A.LoadEntry;
   197	
   198	        D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;
   199	
   200	        /* cpx */
   201	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_CPX, LoadX->AM, LoadX->Arg, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   202	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   203	
   204	        /* bne L */
   205	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_BNE, AM65_BRA, L->Name, L, D->OpEntry->LI);
   206	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   207	
   208	        /* cmp */
   209	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_CMP, LoadA->AM, LoadA->Arg, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   210	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   211	
   212	        /* Rhs load entries must be removed */
   213	        D->Rhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
   214	        D->Rhs.A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
   215	
   216	    } else if ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0 &&
   217	               (D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0) {
   218	
   219	        D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;
   220	
   221	        /* Add operand for low byte */
   222	        AddOpLow (D, OP65_CMP, &D->Rhs);
   223	
   224	        /* bne L */
   225	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_BNE, AM65_BRA, L->Name, L, D->OpEntry->LI);
   226	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   227	
   228	        /* Add operand for high byte */
   229	        AddOpHigh (D, OP65_CMP, &D->Rhs, 0);
   230	
   231	    } else {
   232	
   233	        /* Save lhs into zeropage, then compare */
   234	        AddStoreLhsX (D);
   235	        AddStoreLhsA (D);
   236	
   237	        D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;
   238	
   239	        /* cpx */
   240	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_CPX, AM65_ZP, D->ZPHi, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   241	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   242	
   243	        /* bne L */
   244	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_BNE, AM65_BRA, L->Name, L, D->OpEntry->LI);
   245	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   246	
   247	        /* cmp */
   248	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_CMP, AM65_ZP, D->ZPLo, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   249	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   250	
   251	    }
   252	
   253	    /* Remove the push and the call to the tosgeax function */
   254	    RemoveRemainders (D);
   255	
   256	    /* We changed the sequence */
   257	    return 1;
   258	}
   259	
   260	
   261	
   262	static unsigned Opt_tosshift (StackOpData* D, const char* Name)
   263	/* Optimize shift sequences. */
   264	{
   265	    CodeEntry*  X;
   266	
   267	    /* If the lhs is direct (but not stack relative), we can just reload the
   268	    ** data later.
   269	    */
   270	    if ((D->Lhs.A.Flags & (LI_DIRECT | LI_RELOAD_Y)) == LI_DIRECT &&
   271	        (D->Lhs.X.Flags & (LI_DIRECT | LI_RELOAD_Y)) == LI_DIRECT) {
   272	
   273	        CodeEntry* LoadX = D->Lhs.X.LoadEntry;
   274	        CodeEntry* LoadA = D->Lhs.A.LoadEntry;
   275	
   276	        /* Inline the shift */
   277	        D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;
   278	
   279	        /* tay */
   280	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_TAY, AM65_IMP, 0, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   281	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   282	
   283	        /* lda */
   284	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDA, LoadA->AM, LoadA->Arg, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   285	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   286	
   287	        /* ldx */
   288	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDX, LoadX->AM, LoadX->Arg, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   289	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   290	
   291	        /* Lhs load entries can be removed if not used later */
   292	        D->Lhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
   293	        D->Lhs.A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
   294	
   295	    } else {
   296	
   297	        /* Save lhs into zeropage and reload later */
   298	        AddStoreLhsX (D);
   299	        AddStoreLhsA (D);
   300	
   301	        /* Be sure to setup IP after adding the stores, otherwise it will get
   302	        ** messed up.
   303	        */
   304	        D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;
   305	
   306	        /* tay */
   307	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_TAY, AM65_IMP, 0, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   308	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   309	
   310	        /* lda zp */
   311	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDA, AM65_ZP, D->ZPLo, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   312	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   313	
   314	        /* ldx zp+1 */
   315	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDX, AM65_ZP, D->ZPHi, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   316	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   317	
   318	    }
   319	
   320	    /* jsr shlaxy/aslaxy/whatever */
   321	    X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_JSR, AM65_ABS, Name, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   322	    InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   323	
   324	    /* Remove the push and the call to the shift function */
   325	    RemoveRemainders (D);
   326	
   327	    /* We changed the sequence */
   328	    return 1;
   329	}
   330	
   331	
   332	
   333	static unsigned Opt___bzero (StackOpData* D)
   334	/* Optimize the __bzero sequence */
   335	{
   336	    CodeEntry*  X;
   337	    const char* Arg;
   338	    CodeLabel*  L;
   339	
   340	    /* Check if we're using a register variable */
   341	    if (!IsRegVar (D)) {
   342	        /* Store the value into the zeropage instead of pushing it */
   343	        AddStoreLhsX (D);
   344	        AddStoreLhsA (D);
   345	    }
   346	
   347	    /* If the return value of __bzero is used, we have to add code to reload
   348	    ** a/x from the pointer variable.
   349	    */
   350	    if (RegAXUsed (D->Code, D->OpIndex+1)) {
   351	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDA, AM65_ZP, D->ZPLo, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   352	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+1);
   353	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDX, AM65_ZP, D->ZPHi, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   354	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+2);
   355	    }
   356	
   357	    /* X is always zero, A contains the size of the data area to zero.
   358	    ** Note: A may be zero, in which case the operation is null op.
   359	    */
   360	    if (D->OpEntry->RI->In.RegA != 0) {
   361	
   362	        /* lda #$00 */
   363	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDA, AM65_IMM, "$00", 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   364	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+1);
   365	
   366	        /* The value of A is known */
   367	        if (D->OpEntry->RI->In.RegA <= 0x81) {
   368	
   369	            /* Loop using the sign bit */
   370	
   371	            /* ldy #count-1 */
   372	            Arg = MakeHexArg (D->OpEntry->RI->In.RegA - 1);
   373	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDY, AM65_IMM, Arg, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   374	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+2);
   375	
   376	            /* L: sta (zp),y */
   377	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_STA, AM65_ZP_INDY, D->ZPLo, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   378	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+3);
   379	            L = CS_GenLabel (D->Code, X);
   380	
   381	            /* dey */
   382	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_DEY, AM65_IMP, 0, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   383	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+4);
   384	
   385	            /* bpl L */
   386	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_BPL, AM65_BRA, L->Name, L, D->OpEntry->LI);
   387	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+5);
   388	
   389	        } else {
   390	
   391	            /* Loop using an explicit compare */
   392	
   393	            /* ldy #$00 */
   394	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDY, AM65_IMM, "$00", 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   395	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+2);
   396	
   397	            /* L: sta (zp),y */
   398	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_STA, AM65_ZP_INDY, D->ZPLo, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   399	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+3);
   400	            L = CS_GenLabel (D->Code, X);
   401	
   402	            /* iny */
   403	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_INY, AM65_IMP, 0, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   404	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+4);
   405	
   406	            /* cpy #count */
   407	            Arg = MakeHexArg (D->OpEntry->RI->In.RegA);
   408	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_CPY, AM65_IMM, Arg, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   409	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+5);
   410	
   411	            /* bne L */
   412	            X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_BNE, AM65_BRA, L->Name, L, D->OpEntry->LI);
   413	            InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+6);
   414	        }
   415	
   416	    }
   417	
   418	    /* Remove the push and the call to the __bzero function */
   419	    RemoveRemainders (D);
   420	
   421	    /* We changed the sequence */
   422	    return 1;
   423	}
   424	
   425	
   426	
   427	static unsigned Opt_staspidx (StackOpData* D)
   428	/* Optimize the staspidx sequence */
   429	{
   430	    CodeEntry* X;
   431	
   432	    /* Check if we're using a register variable */
   433	    if (!IsRegVar (D)) {
   434	        /* Store the value into the zeropage instead of pushing it */
   435	        AddStoreLhsX (D);
   436	        AddStoreLhsA (D);
   437	    }
   438	
   439	    /* Replace the store subroutine call by a direct op */
   440	    X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_STA, AM65_ZP_INDY, D->ZPLo, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   441	    InsertEntry (D, X, D->OpIndex+1);
   442	
   443	    /* Remove the push and the call to the staspidx function */
   444	    RemoveRemainders (D);
   445	
   446	    /* We changed the sequence */
   447	    return 1;
   448	}

   862	/* Optimize the tossubax sequence. Note: subtraction is not commutative! */
   863	{
   864	    CodeEntry*  X;
   865	
   866	
   867	    /* Inline the sbc */
   868	    D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;
   869	
   870	    /* sec */
   871	    X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_SEC, AM65_IMP, 0, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
   872	    InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
   873	
   874	    /* Must be true because of OP_RHS_LOAD */
   875	    CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);
   876	
   877	    /* Add code for low operand */
   878	    AddOpLow (D, OP65_SBC, &D->Rhs);
   879

   881	    AddOpHigh (D, OP65_SBC, &D->Rhs, 1);

   885	    D->Rhs.A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;

   888	    RemoveRemainders (D);

   891	    return 1;

  1164	static unsigned Opt_a_toscmpbool (StackOpData* D, const char* BoolTransformer)
  1165	/* Optimize the TOS compare sequence with a bool transformer */
  1166	{
  1167	    CodeEntry* X;
  1168	    cmp_t      Cond;
  1169	
  1170	    D->IP = D->OpIndex + 1;
  1171	
  1172	    if (!D->RhsMultiChg                     &&
  1173	        (D->Rhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0   &&
  1174	        (D->Rhs.A.LoadEntry->Flags & CEF_DONT_REMOVE) == 0) {
  1175	
  1176	        /* cmp */
  1177	        AddOpLow (D, OP65_CMP, &D->Rhs);
  1178	
  1179	        /* Rhs low-byte load must be removed and hi-byte load may be removed */
  1180	        D->Rhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
  1181	        D->Rhs.A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
  1182	
  1183	    } else if ((D->Lhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0) {
  1184	        /* If the lhs is direct (but not stack relative), encode compares with lhs,
  1185	        ** effectively reversing the order (which doesn't matter for == and !=).
  1186	        */
  1187	        Cond = FindBoolCmpCond (BoolTransformer);
  1188	        Cond = GetRevertedCond (Cond);
  1189	        BoolTransformer = GetBoolTransformer (Cond);
  1190	
  1191	        /* This shouldn't fail */
  1192	        CHECK (BoolTransformer);
  1193	
  1194	        /* cmp */
  1195	        AddOpLow (D, OP65_CMP, &D->Lhs);
  1196	
  1197	        /* Lhs load entries can be removed if not used later */
  1198	        D->Lhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
  1199	        D->Lhs.A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
  1200	
  1201	    } else {
  1202	        /* We'll do reverse-compare */
  1203	        Cond = FindBoolCmpCond (BoolTransformer);
  1204	        Cond = GetRevertedCond (Cond);
  1205	        BoolTransformer = GetBoolTransformer (Cond);
  1206	
  1207	        /* This shouldn't fail */
  1208	        CHECK (BoolTransformer);
  1209	
  1210	        /* Save lhs into zeropage */
  1211	        AddStoreLhsA (D);
  1212	        /* AddStoreLhsA may have moved the OpIndex, recalculate insertion point to prevent label migration. */
  1213	        D->IP = D->OpIndex + 1;
  1214	
  1215	        /* cmp */
  1216	        X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_CMP, AM65_ZP, D->ZPLo, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
  1217	        InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
  1218	
  1219	    }
  1220	
  1221	    /* Create a call to the boolean transformer function. This is needed for all
  1222	    ** variants.
  1223	    */
  1224	    X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_JSR, AM65_ABS, BoolTransformer, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
  1225	    InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);
  1226	
  1227	    /* Remove the push and the call to the TOS function */
  1228	    RemoveRemainders (D);
  1229	
  1230	    /* We changed the sequence */
  1231	    return 1;
  1232	}

  1537	/* Check if the preconditions for a call to the optimizer subfunction are
  1538	** satisfied. As a side effect, this function will also choose the zero page

  1564	    HiVal = D->OpEntry->RI->In.RegX;
  1565	    /* Check normally first, then interchange A/X and check again if necessary */
  1566	    for (I = (Desc->Flags & OP_AX_INTERCHANGE ? 0 : 1); !Passed && I < 2; ++I) {
  1567	
  1568	        do {
  1569	            if ((Desc->Flags & OP_A_KNOWN) != 0 &&
  1570	                RegValIsUnknown (LoVal)) {
  1571	                /* Cannot optimize */
  1572	                break;
  1573	            }
  1574	            if ((Desc->Flags & OP_X_ZERO) != 0 &&
  1575	                HiVal != 0) {
  1576	                /* Cannot optimize */
  1577	                break;
  1578	            }
  1579	            Passed = 1;
  1580	        } while (0);
  1581	
  1582	        /* Interchange A/X */
  1583	        LoVal = D->OpEntry->RI->In.RegX;
  1584	        HiVal = D->OpEntry->RI->In.RegA;
  1585	    }
  1586	    if (!Passed) {
  1587	        /* Cannot optimize */
  1588	        return 0;
  1589	    }
  1590	
  1591	    Passed = 0;
  1592	    Lhs = &D->Lhs;
  1593	    Rhs = &D->Rhs;
  1594	    /* Check normally first, then interchange LHS/RHS and check again if necessary */
  1595	    for (I = (Desc->Flags & OP_LR_INTERCHANGE ? 0 : 1); !Passed && I < 2; ++I) {
  1596	
  1597	        do {
  1598	            LhsLo = &Lhs->A;
  1599	            LhsHi = &Lhs->X;
  1600	            RhsLo = &Rhs->A;
  1601	            RhsHi = &Rhs->X;
  1602	            /* Currently we have only LHS/RHS checks with identical requirements for A/X,
  1603	            ** so we don't need to check twice for now.
  1604	            */
  1605	
  1606	            if ((Desc->Flags & OP_LHS_LOAD) != 0) {
  1607	                if ((LhsLo->Flags & LhsHi->Flags & LI_LOAD_INSN) == 0) {
  1608	                    /* Cannot optimize */
  1609	                    break;
  1610	                } else if ((Desc->Flags & OP_LHS_LOAD_DIRECT) != 0) {
  1611	                    if ((LhsLo->Flags & LhsHi->Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0) {
  1612	                        /* Cannot optimize */
  1613	                        break;
  1614	                    }
  1615	                }
  1616	            }
  1617	            if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD) != 0) {
  1618	                if ((RhsLo->Flags & RhsHi->Flags & LI_LOAD_INSN) == 0) {
  1619	                    /* Cannot optimize */
  1620	                    break;
  1621	                } else if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT) != 0) {
  1622	                    if ((RhsLo->Flags & RhsHi->Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0) {
  1623	                        /* Cannot optimize */
  1624	                        break;
  1625	                    }
  1626	                }
  1627	            }
  1628	            if ((Desc->Flags & OP_LHS_REMOVE) != 0) {
  1629	                /* Check if the load entries cannot be removed */
  1630	                if ((LhsLo->LoadEntry != 0 && (LhsLo->LoadEntry->Flags & CEF_DONT_REMOVE) != 0) ||
  1631	                    (LhsHi->LoadEntry != 0 && (LhsHi->LoadEntry->Flags & CEF_DONT_REMOVE) != 0)) {
  1632	                    if ((Desc->Flags & OP_LHS_REMOVE_DIRECT) != 0) {
  1633	                        /* Cannot optimize */
  1634	                        break;
  1635	                    }
  1636	                }
  1637	            }
  1638	            if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_REMOVE) != 0) {
  1639	                if ((RhsLo->LoadEntry != 0 && (RhsLo->LoadEntry->Flags & CEF_DONT_REMOVE) != 0) ||
  1640	                    (RhsHi->LoadEntry != 0 && (RhsHi->LoadEntry->Flags & CEF_DONT_REMOVE) != 0)) {
  1641	                    if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT) != 0) {
  1642	                        /* Cannot optimize */
  1643	                        break;
  1644	                    }
  1645	                }
  1646	            }
  1647	            if (D->RhsMultiChg && (Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT) != 0) {
  1648	                /* Cannot optimize */
  1649	                break;
  1650	            }
  1651	            Passed = 1;
  1652	        } while (0);
  1653	
  1654	        /* Interchange LHS/RHS for next round */
  1655	        Lhs = &D->Rhs;
  1656	        Rhs = &D->Lhs;
  1657	    }
  1658	    if (!Passed) {
  1659	        /* Cannot optimize */
  1660	        return 0;
  1661	    }
  1662	
  1663	    /* Determine the zero page locations to use. We've tracked the used
  1664	    ** ZP locations, so try to find some for us that are unused.
  1665	    */
  1666	    if ((D->ZPUsage & REG_PTR1) == REG_NONE) {
  1667	        D->ZPLo = "ptr1";
  1668	        D->ZPHi = "ptr1+1";
  1669	    } else if ((D->ZPUsage & REG_SREG) == REG_NONE) {
  1670	        D->ZPLo = "sreg";
  1671	        D->ZPHi = "sreg+1";
  1672	    } else if ((D->ZPUsage & REG_PTR2) == REG_NONE) {
  1673	        D->ZPLo = "ptr2";
  1674	        D->ZPHi = "ptr2+1";
  1675	    } else {
  1676	        /* No registers available */
  1677	        return 0;
  1678	    }
  1679	
  1680	    /* Determine if we have a basic block */
  1681	    return CS_IsBasicBlock (D->Code, D->PushIndex, D->OpIndex);
  1682	}

  1847	unsigned OptStackOps (CodeSeg* S)
  1848	/* Optimize operations that take operands via the stack */
  1849	{
  1850	    unsigned        Changes = 0;        /* Number of changes in one run */
  1851	    StackOpData     Data;
  1852	    int             I;
  1853	    int             OldEntryCount;      /* Old number of entries */
  1854	    unsigned        Used;               /* What registers would be used */
  1855	    unsigned        PushedRegs = 0;     /* Track if the same regs are used after the push */
  1856	    int             RhsAChgIndex;       /* Track if rhs is changed more than once */
  1857	    int             RhsXChgIndex;       /* Track if rhs is changed more than once */
  1858	    int             IsRegAOptFunc = 0;  /* Whether to use the RegA-only optimizations */
  1859	
  1860	    enum {
  1861	        Initialize,
  1862	        Search,
  1863	        FoundPush,
  1864	        FoundOp
  1865	    } State = Initialize;
  1866	
  1867	
  1868	    /* Remember the code segment in the info struct */
  1869	    Data.Code = S;
  1870	
  1871	    /* Look for a call to pushax followed by a call to some other function
  1872	    ** that takes it's first argument on the stack, and the second argument
  1873	    ** in the primary register.
  1874	    ** It depends on the code between the two if we can handle/transform the
  1875	    ** sequence, so check this code for the following list of things:
  1876	    **
  1877	    **  - the range must be a basic block (one entry, one exit)
  1878	    **  - there may not be accesses to local variables with unknown
  1879	    **    offsets (because we have to adjust these offsets).

  1881	    **  - no jump labels
  1882	    **
  1883	    ** Since we need a zero page register later, do also check the
  1884	    ** intermediate code for zero page use.
  1885	    ** When hibytes of both oprands are equal, we may have more specialized
  1886	    ** optimization for the op.
  1887	    */

  1891	        /* Get the next entry */
  1892	        CodeEntry* E = CS_GetEntry (S, I);
  1893	
  1894	        /* Actions depend on state */
  1895	        switch (State) {
  1896	
  1897	            case Initialize:
  1898	                ResetStackOpData (&Data);
  1899	                State = Search;
  1900	                /* FALLTHROUGH */
  1901	
  1902	            case Search:
  1903	                /* While searching, track register load insns, so we can tell
  1904	                ** what is in a register once pushax is encountered.
  1905	                */
  1906	                if (CE_HasLabel (E)) {
  1907	                    /* Currently we don't track across branches.
  1908	                    ** Treat this as a change to all regs.
  1909	                    */
  1910	                    ClearLoadInfo (&Data.Lhs);
  1911	                    Data.Lhs.A.ChgIndex = I;
  1912	                    Data.Lhs.X.ChgIndex = I;
  1913	                    Data.Lhs.Y.ChgIndex = I;
  1914	                }
  1915	                if (CE_IsCallTo (E, "pushax")) {
  1916	                    /* Disallow removing Lhs loads if the registers are used */
  1917	                    SetIfOperandLoadUnremovable (&Data.Lhs, Data.UsedRegs);
  1918	
  1919	                    /* The Lhs regs are also used as the default Rhs until changed */
  1920	                    PushedRegs = REG_AXY;
  1921	                    CopyLoadInfo (&Data.Rhs, &Data.Lhs);
  1922	
  1923	                    Data.PushIndex = I;
  1924	                    Data.PushEntry = E;
  1925	                    State = FoundPush;
  1926	                } else {
  1927	                    /* Track load insns */
  1928	                    Used = TrackLoads (&Data.Lhs, S, I);
  1929	                    Data.UsedRegs &= ~E->Chg;
  1930	                    Data.UsedRegs |= Used;
  1931	                }
  1932	                break;
  1933	
  1934	            case FoundPush:
  1935	                /* We' found a pushax before. Search for a stack op that may
  1936	                ** follow and in the meantime, track zeropage usage and check
  1937	                ** for code that will disable us from translating the sequence.
  1938	                */
  1939	                if (CE_HasLabel (E)) {
  1940	                    /* Currently we don't track across branches.
  1941	                    ** Treat this as a change to all regs.
  1942	                    */
  1943	                    ClearLoadInfo (&Data.Rhs);
  1944	                    Data.Rhs.A.ChgIndex = I;
  1945	                    Data.Rhs.X.ChgIndex = I;
  1946	                    Data.Rhs.Y.ChgIndex = I;
  1947	                }
  1948	                if (E->OPC == OP65_JSR) {
  1949	                    /* Subroutine call: Check if this is one of the functions,
  1950	                    ** we're going to replace.
  1951	                    */
  1952	                    if (SameRegXValue (&Data)) {
  1953	                        Data.OptFunc = FindFunc (FuncRegATable, FUNC_COUNT (FuncRegATable), E->Arg);
  1954	                        IsRegAOptFunc = 1;
  1955	                    }
  1956	                    if (Data.OptFunc == 0) {
  1957	                        Data.OptFunc = FindFunc (FuncTable, FUNC_COUNT (FuncTable), E->Arg);
  1958	                        IsRegAOptFunc = 0;
  1959	                    }
  1960	                    if (Data.OptFunc) {
  1961	                        /* Disallow removing Rhs loads if the registers are used */
  1962	                        SetIfOperandLoadUnremovable (&Data.Rhs, Data.UsedRegs);
  1963	
  1964	                        /* Remember the op index and go on */
  1965	                        Data.OpIndex = I;
  1966	                        Data.OpEntry = E;
  1967	                        State = FoundOp;
  1968	                        break;
  1969	                    } else if (!HarmlessCall (E, 2)) {
  1970	                        /* The call might use or change the content that we are
  1971	                        ** going to access later via the stack pointer. In any
  1972	                        ** case, we need to start over after the last pushax.
  1973	                        ** Note: This will also happen if we encounter a call
  1974	                        ** to pushax!
  1975	                        */
  1976	                        I = Data.PushIndex;
  1977	                        State = Initialize;
  1978	                        break;
  1979	                    }
  1980	                } else if (((E->Chg | E->Use) & REG_SP) != 0) {
  1981	
  1982	                    /* If we are using the stack, and we don't have "indirect Y"
  1983	                    ** addressing mode, or the value of Y is unknown, or less
  1984	                    ** than two, we cannot cope with this piece of code. Having
  1985	                    ** an unknown value of Y means that we cannot correct the
  1986	                    ** stack offset, while having an offset less than two means
  1987	                    ** that the code works with the value on stack which is to
  1988	                    ** be removed.
  1989	                    */
  1990	                    if (E->AM == AM65_ZPX_IND               ||
  1991	                        ((E->Chg | E->Use) & SLV_IND) == 0  ||
  1992	                        (RegValIsUnknown (E->RI->In.RegY)   ||
  1993	                         E->RI->In.RegY < 2)) {
  1994	                        I = Data.PushIndex;
  1995	                        State = Initialize;
  1996	                        break;
  1997	                    }
  1998	
  1999	                }
  2000	
  2001	                /* Memorize the old rhs load indices before refreshing them */
  2002	                RhsAChgIndex = Data.Rhs.A.ChgIndex;
  2003	                RhsXChgIndex = Data.Rhs.X.ChgIndex;

Now I understand the issue better. Let me look at the `Opt_a_tosbitwise` function: it handles the case where `(D->Rhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0` - it falls back to using LHS or storing to ZP. But `Opt_a_tossub` doesn't have such a fallback - it just asserts that both A and X have `LI_DIRECT`.

The issue is that `Opt_a_tossub` has `OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` flags, but the assert at line 1377 requires both `Rhs.A.Flags` and `Rhs.X.Flags` to have `LI_DIRECT`. However, the precondition check `RegAPreCondOk` at line 1774-1783 only checks `RhsLo->Flags` (which is A) for `LI_LOAD_INSN` and `LI_DIRECT`, but does NOT check `RhsHi` (X). But the function itself assumes both A and X are direct.

Wait, but looking at `Opt_a_tosbitwise` (which has same flags `OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`), it too has a `CHECK` at a similar position? Let me check:

`Opt_a_tosbitwise` doesn't have a CHECK for both A and X being LI_DIRECT. It handles the case where `(D->Rhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0`. But it does assume X is direct if it's used.

Let me look at the `Opt_a_tosand` entry in the table again:

```
{ "tosandax",   Opt_a_tosand,  REG_NONE, OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT },
```

So `Opt_a_tosand` calls `Opt_a_tosbitwise(D, OP65_AND)`. Let me check if `Opt_a_tosbitwise` has a CHECK similar to line 1377... No, it doesn't. It gracefully handles cases where `LI_DIRECT` is not set for A.

Now, the problem with `Opt_a_tossub`: it has the same flags `OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`, but it asserts that both A and X have `LI_DIRECT`, while the precondition check in `RegAPreCondOk` only checks A (not X) for `LI_DIRECT`. Wait, actually let me re-read the precondition check...

Looking at `RegAPreCondOk` lines 1774-1783:
```c
if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD) != 0) {
    if ((RhsLo->Flags & LI_LOAD_INSN) == 0) {
        /* Cannot optimize */
        break;
    } else if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT) != 0) {
        if ((RhsLo->Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0) {
            /* Cannot optimize */
            break;
        }
    }
}
```

This only checks `RhsLo` (which is A). It doesn't check `RhsHi` (X). But the assert in `Opt_a_tossub` checks both A and X. So if X is not `LI_DIRECT` but A is, the precondition passes but the assert fails.

But wait, `Opt_a_tossub` is the "RegA-only" variant (it's in `FuncRegATable`). The RegA-only functions are only supposed to care about A register because X is assumed to be the same as the push's X value. Let me verify this by looking at `SameRegXValue`:

Actually, looking at line 1952:
```c
if (SameRegXValue (&Data)) {
    Data.OptFunc = FindFunc (FuncRegATable, ...);
    IsRegAOptFunc = 1;
}
```

So `FuncRegATable` entries are only used when `SameRegXValue` returns true. That means the high bytes (X) of LHS and RHS are the same. In that case, the subtract operation only needs to operate on the low byte (A). So `Opt_a_tossub` only needs the low byte of RHS to be direct.

But then why does `Opt_a_tossub` check both A and X for `LI_DIRECT`? Let me re-read it:

```c
/* Must be true because of OP_RHS_LOAD */
CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);
```

The comment says "Must be true because of OP_RHS_LOAD". But the precondition `RegAPreCondOk` only checks `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` for A (not X). So there's a mismatch: either the CHECK is too strict, or the precondition check is too lax.

Looking at `Opt_a_tossub`, it does:
1. `AddOpLow(D, OP65_SBC, &D->Rhs)` - this needs RHS.A to be direct
2. Sign extension for X if X is used

But it doesn't use `D->Rhs.X` directly! It only uses `D->Rhs.A`. The X part is handled by the sign extension code (lines 1387-1404). So the CHECK requiring both A and X to be LI_DIRECT is wrong - it should only check A.

2026-05-29 01:24:13,496 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the issue. Let me trace through what happens:

1. `Opt_a_tossub` is the RegA-only variant. It's called when `SameRegXValue` returns true (i.e., high bytes of LHS and RHS are the same).

2. For subtraction `a = c - (d >= 0)`:
   - `c` is 10, `d >= 0` is always true (1). So this is `10 - 1 = 9`.
   - The high bytes are both 0 (since these are small unsigned char values).
   - So `SameRegXValue` returns true, and `Opt_a_tossub` is selected.

3. `Opt_a_tossub` asserts `CHECK((D->Rhs.A.Flags & D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0)`. It requires BOTH A and X to be LI_DIRECT.

4. But the precondition check `RegAPreCondOk` only requires `Rhs.A` (low byte) to be `LI_DIRECT` through `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`. It does NOT require `Rhs.X` to be `LI_DIRECT`.

5. In the test case, `d >= 0` is a constant expression (always true), so the RHS might not have a direct load for X (it's just an immediate `LDX #$00` or something similar that may or may not be LI_DIRECT).

Actually, let me look at what happens with `(d >= 0)`. Since `d >= 0` is always true, the compiler evaluates it to constant 1. So the RHS is the constant 1 (which is `A=1, X=0`). But the question is: does the RHS have LI_DIRECT set for both A and X?

The problem is that `Opt_a_tossub` uses `AddOpLow(D, OP65_SBC, &D->Rhs)` which only needs `Rhs.A` to be direct. It does NOT need `Rhs.X` at all! The X part is handled separately via sign extension (lines 1387-1404). So the CHECK requiring both A and X to be LI_DIRECT is too strict.

But wait, there's also the issue that `AddOpLow` calls `LI->A.Flags` - it only uses A. So the function only needs `Rhs.A` to be `LI_DIRECT`.

Now, `Opt_tossubax` (the non-A variant, line 861) does need both A and X because it calls both `AddOpLow` and `AddOpHigh`. The `Opt_a_tossub` only calls `AddOpLow` and handles X via sign extension.

So the fix should be to change the CHECK in `Opt_a_tossub` to only check A (not X), and possibly also check that we have a fallback if A is not LI_DIRECT (like `Opt_a_tosbitwise` does).

But actually, the precondition `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` ensures that `Rhs.A` is `LI_DIRECT`. So we just need to fix the CHECK to only check A:

```c
CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);
```

But wait, there's another issue. Look at `Opt_a_tossub` again:

```c
static unsigned Opt_a_tossub (StackOpData* D)
/* Optimize the tossubax sequence. */
{
    CodeEntry*  X;

    /* Inline the sbc */
    D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;

    /* Must be true because of OP_RHS_LOAD */
    CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);

    /* sec */
    X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_SEC, AM65_IMP, 0, 0, D->OpEntry->LI);
    InsertEntry (D, X, D->IP++);

    /* Add code for low operand */
    AddOpLow (D, OP65_SBC, &D->Rhs);

    /* Do sign-extension as high-byte operation only when its result is used */
    if ((GetRegInfo (D->Code, D->IP, REG_X) & REG_X) != 0) {
        ...
    }

    /* Rhs load entries must be removed */
    D->Rhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
    D->Rhs.A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;

    /* Remove the push and the call to the tossubax function */
    RemoveRemainders (D);

    /* We changed the sequence */
    return 1;
}
```

The function:
1. Uses `AddOpLow(D, OP65_SBC, &D->Rhs)` which needs `Rhs.A` to be `LI_DIRECT` (or falls back to ZP)
2. Handles X via sign extension
3. Removes both Rhs.A and Rhs.X loads

So the fix should be to change the CHECK to only check A (since that's what the function actually needs), and also handle the case where `Rhs.A` is not `LI_DIRECT` (by using ZP storage like `Opt_a_tosbitwise` does).

But actually, looking at `AddOpLow`, it already handles the case where `LI_DIRECT` is not set (lines 1072-1077): it uses `AM65_ZP` with `D->ZPLo`. So `AddOpLow` already has a fallback! The CHECK is just overly strict.

Let me also look at `Opt_a_toscmpbool` which is used by the comparison functions (`tosgeax`, `tosleax`, etc.). It has `OP_NONE` flags (no requirement for RHS to be direct) and handles the non-direct case gracefully.

Now let me create a test to reproduce the issue first

   223	static int Affected (LoadRegInfo* LRI, const CodeEntry* E)
   224	/* Check if the result of the same loading code as in LRI may be changed by E.
   225	** If any part of the arg is used, it could be unsafe to add such a store before E.
   226	** If any part of the arg is changed, it could be unsafe to add such a load after E.
   227	*/
   228	{
   229	    fncls_t         fncls;
   230	    unsigned int    Use;
   231	    unsigned int    Chg;
   232	    unsigned int    UseToCheck = 0;
   233	    unsigned int    ChgToCheck = 0;
   234	    const ZPInfo*   ZI  = 0;
   235	    unsigned        Res = 0;
   236	    CodeEntry*      AE  = 0;
   237	    CodeEntry*      YE  = 0;

   245	        goto L_Result;

   249	
   250	    if ((LRI->Flags & LI_CHECK_ARG) != 0) {
   251	        AE = LRI->LoadEntry;
   252	        if (AE != 0) {

   255	            */

   268	                ChgToCheck |= ZI->ByteUse;
   269	            }
   270	        } else {
   271	            /* We don't know what regs could have been used for the src.
   272	            ** So we just assume all.
   273	            */

   123	void AdjustLoadRegInfo (LoadRegInfo* LRI, int Index, int Change)
   124	/* Adjust a load register info struct after deleting or inserting an entry
   125	** with a given index
   126	*/
   127	{
   128	    CHECK (abs (Change) == 1);
   129	    if (Change < 0) {
   130	        /* Deletion */
   131	        if (Index < LRI->LoadIndex) {
   132	            --LRI->LoadIndex;
   133	        } else if (Index == LRI->LoadIndex) {
   134	            /* Has been removed */
   135	            LRI->LoadIndex = -1;
   136	            LRI->LoadEntry = 0;
   137	        }
   138	        if (Index < LRI->LoadYIndex) {
   139	            --LRI->LoadIndex;
   140	        } else if (Index == LRI->LoadYIndex) {
   141	            /* Has been removed */
   142	            LRI->LoadYIndex = -1;
   143	            LRI->LoadYEntry = 0;
   144	        }
   145	        if (Index < LRI->ChgIndex) {
   146	            --LRI->ChgIndex;
   147	        } else if (Index == LRI->ChgIndex) {
   148	            /* Has been removed */
   149	            LRI->ChgIndex = -1;
   150	            LRI->ChgEntry = 0;
   151	        }
   152	    } else {
   153	        /* Insertion */
   154	        if (Index <= LRI->LoadIndex) {
   155	            ++LRI->LoadIndex;
   156	        }
   157	        if (Index <= LRI->LoadYIndex) {
   158	            ++LRI->LoadYIndex;
   159	        }
   160	        if (Index <= LRI->ChgIndex) {
   161	            ++LRI->ChgIndex;
   162	        }
   163	    }
   164	}

So `LI_DIRECT` is set in `FinalizeLoadRegInfo` at line 106-108 when the source hasn't been changed and there's a check arg/check Y flag. It can be cleared at line 117 if there's an issue with Y.

Now, let me think about the specific bug. When we have:
```c
a = c - (d >= 0);
```

The RHS `(d >= 0)` is a constant `1` (since `d` is unsigned, `d >= 0` is always true). So the compiler evaluates this to `1`. But the load for this constant might be:
- `LDA #$01` (for the low byte, A)
- `LDX #$00` (for the high byte, X)

Now, `SameRegXValue` compares the X values of LHS and RHS. Since both are 0, it returns true, and the RegA-only path is chosen.

Then `RegAPreCondOk` checks:
- `OP_RHS_LOAD`: `Rhs.A.Flags & LI_LOAD_INSN` must be set
- `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`: `Rhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT` must be set

But it does NOT check `Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT`. So if `Rhs.X` doesn't have `LI_DIRECT` (maybe because it's an immediate load that got flagged differently), the precondition passes but the CHECK fails.

Wait, let me check: does an immediate load `LDX #$00` get `LI_DIRECT`?

So for `AM65_IMM`, `LI_DIRECT` is set immediately (line 551). So an `LDX #$00` would have `LI_DIRECT` set. 

But wait, the problem might be something else. Let me trace through more carefully.

When the RHS is a constant `1` (from `d >= 0`), the compiler generates:
- `LDA #$01` (to load 1 into A)
- `LDX #$00` (to load 0 into X)

Then `pushax` is called to push these values onto the stack.

But wait - the code is `a = c - (d >= 0)`. So `c` is the LHS, and `(d >= 0)` is the RHS. The pushax pushes `c` (LHS) onto the stack, and then the RHS `(d >= 0)` is in A/X. Then `tossubax` is called.

So the flow is:
1. Load `c` (LHS) -> A, X
2. `pushax` (pushes LHS)
3. Load `(d >= 0)` (RHS) -> A, X
4. `tossubax` (subtract RHS from LHS)

Now, the issue is that `(d >= 0)` is a constant 1. The compiler probably generates:
- `LDA #$01`
- `LDX #$00`

But maybe the `LDX #$00` is optimized away or shared with something else?

# ---- Display info during parsing phase ----
SILENT:=$(findstring s,$(word 1, $(MAKEFLAGS)))
ifneq ($(SILENT),s)
    $(info Using Makefile: $(realpath $(firstword $(MAKEFILE_LIST))) $(MAKECMDGOALS))
endif

.SUFFIXES:

all:
	@$(MAKE) -C src         --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C libsrc      --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C doc         --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C util        --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C samples     --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) checkprefix    --no-print-directory

zip:
	@$(MAKE) -C src         --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C libsrc      --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C doc         --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C util        --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C samples     --no-print-directory $@

install:
ifndef PREFIX
ifndef DESTDIR
	$(error Error: PREFIX or DESTDIR must be set for install to work)
endif
endif
	@$(MAKE) -C src        --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C libsrc     --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C doc        --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C util       --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C samples    --no-print-directory $@

mostlyclean clean:
	@$(MAKE) -C src        --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C libsrc     --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C doc        --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C util       --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C samples    --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C test       --no-print-directory $@
	@$(MAKE) -C targettest --no-print-directory $@

2026-05-29 01:26:40,385 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I can see the problem clearly:
- `Rhs.A.Flags = 0x10001` which has `LI_DIRECT` (0x0001) set
- `Rhs.X.Flags = 0x0000` which has NO flags set at all (not even `LI_LOAD_INSN`)

So `Rhs.X` has no load instruction at all! That's because the RHS's X value is the same as LHS's X value (both are 0), so no explicit `LDX` instruction was generated for the RHS. The X value is "inherited" from LHS.

This means:
1. `SameRegXValue` returns true (both X values are 0)
2. The RegA-only path is chosen
3. `RegAPreCondOk` checks `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` only for A (not for X)
4. `Opt_a_tossub` asserts that both A and X have `LI_DIRECT`, but X has no flags at all

The fix should be to change the CHECK in `Opt_a_tossub` to only check A (since the function only uses `Rhs.A` via `AddOpLow`). X is handled separately via sign extension.

But also, there's a deeper issue: the precondition check `RegAPreCondOk` doesn't check X for `LI_DIRECT` when `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` is set. But for the RegA-only functions, this is correct: they don't need X to be direct because X is the same as LHS's X (which is already on the stack). The RegA-only functions only operate on A.

So the fix is simply to change the CHECK in `Opt_a_tossub` from:
```c
CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);
```
to:
```c
CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);
```

But wait, let me also check if there are other functions with similar issues. Let me check all the CHECK lines in `Opt_a_tos*` functions:

Looking at the grep output earlier, lines 710, 768, 875, 906, 949, 996, 1043, and 1377 have the same CHECK pattern. Let me check which of these are in `Opt_a_*` functions vs `Opt_*` functions:

- Line 710: Let me check
- Line 768: Let me check

- Line 906: `Opt_tosugeax` (non-A variant) - needs both A and X

```c
    ...
}
```

This gracefully handles the case where `Rhs.A` is not `LI_DIRECT`. But for `Opt_a_tossub`, the precondition `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` should guarantee `Rhs.A` has `LI_DIRECT`. However, the bug report shows that the precondition passes but the CHECK fails because X doesn't have `LI_DIRECT`.

So the minimal fix is to change the CHECK. But let me also consider: should the precondition also be fixed? Currently `RegAPreCondOk` checks `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` only for A. But the flag `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` is used for both `Opt_a_tossub` (which only needs A) and `Opt_a_tosand`/`Opt_a_tosor`/`Opt_a_tosxor` (which also only need A). So the precondition is correct for the RegA-only functions.

But there's also the non-RegA table (`FuncTable`) where `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` is used for `tosgeax`, `tosltax`, `tossubax`, `tosugeax`, `tosugtax`, `tosuleax`, `tosultax`. For those, `PreCondOk` checks both A and X (lines 1617-1626):
```c
if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD) != 0) {
    if ((RhsLo->Flags & RhsHi->Flags & LI_LOAD_INSN) == 0) {
        /* Cannot optimize */
        break;
    } else if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT) != 0) {
        if ((RhsLo->Flags & RhsHi->Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0) {
            /* Cannot optimize */
            break;
        }
    }
}
```

Note: `RhsLo->Flags & RhsHi->Flags` - this is bitwise AND of the two flags, then checking if `LI_LOAD_INSN` is set in the result. This requires BOTH to have `LI_LOAD_INSN`. And similarly for `LI_DIRECT`. So for non-RegA functions, both A and X must have `LI_DIRECT`.

For RegA functions (`RegAPreCondOk`), the check is only on `RhsLo` (A):
```c
if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD) != 0) {
    if ((RhsLo->Flags & LI_LOAD_INSN) == 0) {
        /* Cannot optimize */
        break;
    } else if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT) != 0) {
        if ((RhsLo->Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0) {
            /* Cannot optimize */
            break;
        }
    }
}
```

This only checks A, not X. So the precondition is correct for RegA functions (they only need A to be direct). But the CHECK in `Opt_a_tossub` incorrectly requires both.

Now let me fix this:



🎬 ACTION

@@ -1374,10 +1374,6 @@ static unsigned Opt_a_tossub (StackOpData* D)
     D->IP = D->OpIndex+1;

Let me check the optimized code more carefully. The issue is that it's loading `_b` instead of `_c`. This might be because the optimizer incorrectly uses the LHS from the wrong place.

Actually wait, let me re-examine the optimized output:
```
lda     _b
beq     L0003
lda     #$00
sta     _b
L0003:  sec
sbc     #$01
sta     _a
cmp     #$09
jmp     boolne
```

The `lda _b` is from the `if (b != 0)` check. Then `beq L0003` branches to L0003. At L0003, the code does `sec; sbc #$01`. But where does the value of `c` get loaded?

Looking at the non-optimized version:
```
ldx     #$00
lda     _b
cmp     #$00
jsr     boolne
jeq     L0002
ldx     #$00
lda     #$00
sta     _b
L0002:  ldx     #$00
lda     _c
jsr     pushax
ldx     #$00
lda     #$01
jsr     tossubax
...
```

The optimized version seems to have merged the `if` and the subtraction incorrectly. The `lda _b` is from the `if` condition, and then after branching to L0003, it should load `_c` but it doesn't.

This is a different bug from what we fixed! The optimized output is semantically wrong. Let me check if this was happening before my fix too (by using an older binary):

Actually, the original error was that the CHECK failed, which means the optimization was NOT applied before my fix. Now with my fix, the optimization IS applied, but it produces wrong code.

So my fix just removes the assertion, but there's still an underlying bug: the `Opt_a_tossub` function assumes things that may not be true, and produces wrong code when the precondition isn't fully met.

The issue is that `RegAPreCondOk` doesn't check that `Rhs.X` has `LI_LOAD_INSN` when `OP_RHS_LOAD` is set. But `OP_RHS_LOAD` requires `LI_LOAD_INSN` on both A and X for the non-RegA path. For the RegA path, maybe it should only require it on A.

But wait, `Opt_a_tossub` uses `D->Rhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE` at line 1407, which means it tries to remove the X load entry. If `Rhs.X` has no load entry (flags = 0), this might not cause issues directly, but the removal logic might fail or do nothing.

The `Opt_a_tossub` function replaces `pushax` + `tossubax` with inline code. The `pushax` is what put `c` on the stack. If the optimization removes `pushax` and replaces `tossubax` with `sec; sbc #$01`, then the value of `c` is lost.\n\nBut `Opt_a_tossub` is a RegA-only optimization. It\'s used when the high bytes of LHS and RHS are the same. In that case, it only needs to operate on the low byte. Let me think about this more carefully. The `Opt_a_tossub` function is only called when:
1. `SameRegXValue` returns true (X values of LHS and RHS are the same)
2. `RegAPreCondOk` passes

`SameRegXValue` checks if the X register values are the same between LHS and RHS. If they are, the RegA-only optimization can be used because the high byte subtraction is zero (same - same = 0) and only the low byte matters.

But there's another subtlety: `Opt_a_tossub` replaces `pushax` + `tossubax`. The `pushax` saves both A and X. The `tossubax` pops both and does subtraction. In the RegA-only case, since X is the same for both LHS and RHS, the high byte of the result is determined by sign extension of the low byte.

So `Opt_a_tossub` needs to:
1. Get the low byte of LHS from wherever it was before `pushax`
2. Get the low byte of RHS from wherever it is now
3. Do `sec; sbc RHS_low`
4. Sign-extend to X

But the way the optimizer works, it replaces the entire `pushax` + `tossubax` sequence. The LHS low byte was loaded into A before `pushax`. After removing `pushax` and `tossubax`, the code should:
- Use the LHS load directly (the `lda _c` that was before `pushax`)
- Then do the SBC with RHS

But looking at the optimized output, the `lda _c` is completely missing. It uses `lda _b` instead. This means the optimizer incorrectly identified which load corresponds to the LHS.

Let me check if the LHS load info is being set correctly. The LHS is tracked in `Data.Lhs`. Initially, `Data.Lhs` tracks the loads that happen before `pushax`. But the code between `if` check and `pushax` might confuse the tracking.

Actually, looking at lines 1902-1932 in `OptStackOps`:

```c
case Search:
    if (CE_HasLabel (E)) {
        ClearLoadInfo (&Data.Lhs);
        ...
    }
    if (CE_IsCallTo (E, "pushax")) {
        ...
        State = FoundPush;
    } else {
        Used = TrackLoads (&Data.Lhs, S, I);
        ...
    }
    break;
```

When a label is encountered, the load info is cleared. The `jeq L0002` branches to L0002, but L0002 is after the `if` body. The code at L0002 starts with `ldx #$00; lda _c`. But there's a label at L0002, which clears the load info.

Wait, but the load info is cleared at the label, and then the loads at L0002 are tracked. So the LHS should be properly tracked as `lda _c` and `ldx #$00`.

But in the optimized output, the label L0002 is gone (renamed to L0003). And the code at L0003 doesn't include `lda _c`. So something else is going on.

Maybe the issue is more complex. Let me check if the test file I'm using matches the PR's test file exactly. The PR has:
```
if (b != 0) {
    b = 0;
}
```

And `b` is initialized to 0. So the `if` is always false. The optimizer might remove the entire `if` block and merge things incorrectly.

Let me look at the generated optimized assembly again and compare with the non-optimized:

Non-optimized:
```
ldx     #$00
lda     _b
cmp     #$00
jsr     boolne
jeq     L0002      ; jump if b == 0 (which is always)
ldx     #$00
lda     #$00
sta     _b
L0002:  ldx     #$00
lda     _c
jsr     pushax
...
```

Optimized:
```
lda     _b
beq     L0003      ; branch if b == 0 (always)
lda     #$00
sta     _b
L0003:  sec
sbc     #$01
sta     _a
cmp     #$09
jmp     boolne
```

The optimized version has:
- `lda _b; beq L0003` - the `if` check, simplified (since `boolne` + `jeq` when A=0 means branch if A=0)
- Then `sec; sbc #$01` - this is the subtraction

But the value in A at `sec` is `b` (0), not `c` (10)! The `lda _c` is missing.

This suggests that some OTHER optimization pass (not `OptStackOps`) merged the `lda _b` and the `lda _c` incorrectly. Or maybe `OptStackOps` itself does this incorrectly.

Let me look at what `Opt_a_tossub` actually does. It inserts code at `D->OpIndex+1` (after the `tossubax` call). It does:
1. `sec`
2. `AddOpLow(D, OP65_SBC, &D->Rhs)` - adds `sbc #$01`
3. Sign extension if needed

Then it removes:
- The pushax call
- The tossubax call
- The RHS loads (if LI_REMOVE is set)
- The LHS loads (if LI_REMOVE is set)

But `AddOpLow` adds code that operates on whatever is currently in A. It doesn't reload the LHS. So after the optimization, the result depends on what was in A before the original `pushax`.

The original sequence is:
```
lda _c        ; A = c (10)  <-- this is the LHS load
jsr pushax    ; push A, X
...
lda #$01      ; A = 1 (RHS)
jsr tossubax  ; pop LHS, compute LHS - RHS
```

After optimization:
```
lda _c        ; A = c (10)  <-- should still be here
sec           ; set carry
sbc #$01      ; A = A - 1 - (1 - carry) = 10 - 1 = 9
```

So the `lda _c` should remain. But in the actual optimized output, it's gone. This means either:
1. The LHS load was incorrectly removed by `RemoveRegLoads` (because `LI_REMOVE` was set on LHS)
2. The LHS load was removed by some other optimization

Looking at `Opt_a_tossub`:
```c
/* Rhs load entries must be removed */
D->Rhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
D->Rhs.A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
```

It only removes RHS loads. LHS loads are NOT removed by this function. So the LHS load should remain.

But then `RemoveRemainders` calls `RemoveRegLoads` for both LHS and RHS. If LHS has `LI_REMOVE` set (from some other code), it would be removed.

But who sets `LI_REMOVE` on LHS? Looking at `Opt_a_tossub`, it doesn't. And the `AddOpLow` function sets `LI->A.Flags |= LI_REMOVE` (line 1070), but that's for the RHS (since `AddOpLow(D, OP65_SBC, &D->Rhs)` passes `&D->Rhs`).

So LHS should not have `LI_REMOVE` set. Therefore `RemoveRegLoads` should not remove the LHS load.

Unless... the LHS load was already removed by some earlier optimization pass before `OptStackOps` runs? Or maybe the issue is that the LHS tracking is wrong.

Let me check if there's another optimization that might remove `lda _c`. Looking at the optimized output, `lda _c` is completely gone. But `lda _b` is present. Could the optimizer have changed `lda _c` to `lda _b`? That seems unlikely.

Wait, maybe I'm reading the optimized output wrong. Let me look at it again with fresh eyes:

```
.proc	_main: near

.segment	"CODE"

	lda     _b
	beq     L0003
	lda     #$00
	sta     _b
L0003:	sec
	sbc     #$01
	sta     _a
	cmp     #$09
	jmp     boolne

.endproc
```

The `lda _b` loads b (0). Then `beq L0003` branches (since b=0). At L0003, `sec; sbc #$01` computes 0 - 1 = -1 = 0xFF. Then `sta _a` stores 0xFF to a. Then `cmp #$09` compares with 9, which is not equal. Then `jmp boolne` returns the result of `!=`.

So `a` becomes 0xFF (255), not 9. This is wrong.

But wait, the `lda _b` is for the `if` condition. After the `if`, the code should load `c`. But the optimizer seems to have removed the load of `c` and instead used the value from the `if` condition directly.

Could this be because `OptJumpTarget3` or some other jump optimization moved the label and merged the two paths? The PR description says: "/* 'if' needed to produce a label below, moved by OptJumpTarget3  */"

So `OptJumpTarget3` might be moving the label L0002 to somewhere else, causing the load of `c` to be skipped.

Actually, I think the problem might be unrelated to my fix. My fix just prevents the CHECK from failing. But the underlying issue might be that the optimization shouldn't be applied at all in this case.

Let me check: should the CHECK have prevented this optimization? The CHECK was:
```c
CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);
```

This requires BOTH A and X to have `LI_DIRECT`. If X doesn't have `LI_DIRECT` (which is the case here: `Rhs.X.Flags = 0`), the CHECK fails. So the original code would have aborted at this point, preventing the (possibly incorrect) optimization.

But my fix allows the optimization to proceed even when X doesn't have `LI_DIRECT`. This might produce incorrect code.

So maybe the correct fix is not just to change the CHECK, but to also fix the precondition check `RegAPreCondOk` to properly validate the requirements, or to fix `Opt_a_tossub` to handle the case where `Rhs.X` is not `LI_DIRECT`.

Actually, looking at this more carefully: `Opt_a_tossub` doesn't need `Rhs.X` to be `LI_DIRECT` at all. It only uses `Rhs.A` for the `AddOpLow` call. The X value is handled by sign extension. So the CHECK was overly strict, and my fix is correct.

But the incorrect code generation is a separate issue. Let me check if it's caused by some other optimization interacting badly.

Let me run the compiler with `-O` but without my fix (using the original binary that crashes):

Actually, I can't do that because it crashes. But I can check if the wrong code is generated with `-O` but with some optimizations disabled.

```
beq     L0003
lda     #$00
sta     _b
L0003:  sec
sbc     #$01
sta     _a
cmp     #$09
jmp     boolne
```

There's no `pusha0` or `pushax` in this output! The code has already been fully optimized. The `pusha0`/`tossuba0` was already replaced by some other optimization.

But when I disable `OptStackOps`, the output has `pusha0`/`tossuba0`. So `OptStackOps` must be doing this replacement. But `OptStackOps` only looks for `pushax`, not `pusha0`...

Actually wait, maybe before `OptStackOps` runs, another pass converts `pusha0`/`tossuba0` to `pushax`/`tossubax`? Or maybe `OptStackOps` itself handles this?

Let me look at the code more carefully. The `OptStackOps` searches for `pushax`:
```c

```

But then it looks for `tossubax` in the function tables. If the code has `pusha0`/`tossuba0`, it wouldn't match.

But the `-Oi` output shows no `pushax` or `pusha0`. So the optimization must have happened. Let me check if there's another optimization that handles this.

```

lda     _c
jsr     pushax
ldx     #$00
lda     #$01
jsr     tossubax
```

Yes, the non-optimized code uses `pushax`/`tossubax`. The `-O --disable-opt OptStackOps` version uses `pusha0`/`tossuba0`. So there must be another optimization that converts `pushax` to `pusha0` when X=0, and `tossubax` to `tossuba0` when both X values are 0.

So with full `-O`, the sequence is:
1. Some optimization converts `pushax` to `pusha0` and `tossubax` to `tossuba0`
2. `OptStackOps` tries to optimize `pushax`/`tossubax` but finds `pusha0`/`tossuba0` instead
3. Actually, `OptStackOps` only looks for `pushax`, so it wouldn't match `pusha0`

But the final `-Oi` output has neither `pushax` nor `pusha0`. So `OptStackOps` must have matched something and replaced it.

Wait, maybe I'm wrong about `OptStackOps` not matching `pusha0`. Let me check if `pusha0` is also matched by `CE_IsCallTo(E, "pushax")`? No, that's a string comparison.


So if `Rhs.A` has `LI_DIRECT`, it inserts `sbc (Rhs.A.LoadEntry->Arg)` and marks Rhs.A for removal.

So maybe the correct fix is not just to remove the CHECK, but to also fix the precondition to prevent this case from reaching `Opt_a_tossub`.

Let me look at what the precondition should check. The issue is that `Lhs.X` has no load (Flags=0). For `pushax` to work correctly, both A and X must have been loaded. If X was never loaded, the value pushed is whatever was in X from before. After optimization, the X value is lost (since pushax is removed), but that's fine because the RegA-only optimization doesn't need X.

But the A value MUST be correct. The problem seems to be that the LHS A load is wrong (it's `lda _b` instead of `lda _c`).

How can we detect this? One way: check that Lhs.A has a proper load instruction. The precondition `RegAPreCondOk` doesn't check LHS at all! It only checks RHS and the A/X values. It assumes the LHS is correctly pushed by `pushax`.

But `PreCondOk` (the non-RegA version) does check LHS via `OP_LHS_LOAD` and `OP_LHS_REMOVE`. However, `Opt_a_tossub` uses `OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` which doesn't include any LHS checks.

For the RegA functions, the LHS is supposed to be on the stack (pushed by pushax). The optimization replaces the pushax + op sequence, so the LHS value that was pushed is now used directly from A. This requires that the LHS A value is still available (the load instruction is still there before the optimization point).

But if the LHS tracking is wrong, the wrong value might be used. However, `Opt_a_tossub` doesn't actually use `Lhs.A.LoadEntry` - it only uses `Rhs.A.LoadEntry`. The LHS value comes from whatever is in A at the point where `pushax` was (which is now removed). So if the tracking is wrong about what was in A before `pushax`, the code after optimization will use whatever is currently in A.

Wait, that's exactly the problem! `Opt_a_tossub` replaces `pushax` + `tossubax` with inline code. But it doesn't add any code to reload the LHS. It assumes the LHS is already in A from before the (now removed) `pushax`. So after optimization, the code just flows from whatever was before `pushax` directly into the `sec; sbc #$01`.

If the code before `pushax` was `lda _c`, then A has `c` and the result is `c - 1 = 9`. But if the code before was `lda _b`, then A has `b` (0) and the result is `0 - 1 = -1 = 255`.

So the issue is that the LHS tracking incorrectly identifies `lda _b` as the LHS load instead of `lda _c`.

This is a bug in the tracking logic, not in `Opt_a_tossub` itself. But the CHECK was preventing this bug from manifesting by crashing.

I think the proper fix is to revert the CHECK change and instead fix the precondition `RegAPreCondOk` to reject cases where `Lhs.X` doesn't have `LI_LOAD_INSN`. But wait, that would prevent ALL RegA optimizations where X is inherited, which might be too strict.

Actually, looking at the flags for `Opt_a_tossub`:
```
{ "tossubax",   Opt_a_tossub,  REG_NONE, OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT },
```

The flags are `OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`. There's no `OP_LHS_LOAD` flag, so `RegAPreCondOk` doesn't check LHS at all. But the function relies on LHS being correctly loaded before `pushax`.

Maybe the fix should be to add `OP_LHS_LOAD` to the flags? But then `RegAPreCondOk` would check `Lhs.A` for `LI_LOAD_INSN`, which it has. It wouldn't fix the issue of the wrong load being tracked.

Hmm, let me think about this differently. The original CHECK was:
```c
CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);
```

This requires both Rhs.A and Rhs.X to have LI_DIRECT. But `Opt_a_tossub` only needs Rhs.A to be direct. The X part of RHS is not used because the subtraction only operates on the low byte (the high byte result is determined by sign extension since both high bytes are the same).

So why did the original author write the CHECK to require both? Maybe it was a copy-paste from `Opt_tossubax` (the non-A variant), which does need both.

I believe the correct fix is:
1. Change the CHECK to only check A (as I did)
2. But also ensure the precondition properly validates that the optimization can be correctly applied

But the precondition already ensures `Rhs.A.Flags & LI_DIRECT` through `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`. The issue of wrong LHS tracking is a separate bug.

Actually, looking at the code flow more carefully:

In `OptStackOps`, after `FoundPush`, it continues scanning in `FoundPush` state. But it also tracks Lhs changes:
```c
/* Keep tracking Lhs src if necessary */
SetIfOperandSrcAffected (&Data.Lhs, E);
```

And:
```c

    if ((PushedRegs & E->Use) != 0) {
        SetIfOperandLoadUnremovable (&Data.Lhs, PushedRegs & E->Use);

```

But the issue might be that the LHS tracking was already wrong BEFORE `FoundPush`. The `Search` state tracks loads, but if there's a label, it clears the load info. If the `if` statement creates a label that causes the load info to be cleared at the wrong time, the tracking could be wrong.

Let me check the non-optimized code structure:

```
        ldx     #$00        ; entry 0
        lda     _b          ; entry 1
        cmp     #$00        ; entry 2
        jsr     boolne      ; entry 3
        jeq     L0002       ; entry 4
        ldx     #$00        ; entry 5
        lda     #$00        ; entry 6
        sta     _b          ; entry 7
L0002:  ldx     #$00        ; entry 8
        lda     _c          ; entry 9
        jsr     pushax      ; entry 10
        ldx     #$00        ; entry 11
        lda     #$01        ; entry 12
        jsr     tossubax    ; entry 13
```

Search state:
- Entry 0: `ldx #$00` -> Lhs.X tracked
- Entry 1: `lda _b` -> Lhs.A tracked
- Entry 2: `cmp #$00` -> uses A, so Lhs.A load becomes unremovable? Actually `TrackLoads` just tracks loads, it doesn't mark them unremovable here. But `SetIfOperandLoadUnremovable` is called later.
- Entry 3: `jsr boolne` -> call, might clear things
- Entry 4: `jeq L0002` -> jump, doesn't affect tracking
- Entry 5: `ldx #$00` -> Lhs.X updated
- Entry 6: `lda #$00` -> Lhs.A updated
- Entry 7: `sta _b` -> doesn't affect tracking
- Entry 8: has label -> ClearLoadInfo! Then `ldx #$00` -> Lhs.X = LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_DIRECT
- Entry 9: `lda _c` -> Lhs.A = LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_CHECK_ARG
- Entry 10: `jsr pushax` -> FoundPush

So at FoundPush:
- Lhs.X has LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_DIRECT (from entry 8)
- Lhs.A has LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_CHECK_ARG (from entry 9)

This is correct.

Then FoundPush state:
- Entry 11: `ldx #$00` -> Rhs.X tracked (since Rhs was copied from Lhs, now updated)
- Entry 12: `lda #$01` -> Rhs.A tracked
- Entry 13: `jsr tossubax` -> FoundOp

So at FoundOp:
- Lhs.X = LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_DIRECT (from entry 8)
- Lhs.A = LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_CHECK_ARG (from entry 9)
- Rhs.X = LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_DIRECT (from entry 11)
- Rhs.A = LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_DIRECT (from entry 12)

This all looks correct! The tracking should produce correct results.

```
Rhs.X Flags=0000 LoadIdx=-1 ChgIdx=5
PushIdx=6 OpIdx=8
```

The indices are much smaller (5, 6, 7, 8) compared to my analysis (9, 10, 12, 13). This means many entries were removed by previous optimization passes before `OptStackOps` runs.

So other optimizations (like `OptJumpTarget3`, `OptBool`, etc.) have already transformed the code, removing the `boolne` call, the `cmp`, etc. The code that `OptStackOps` sees is different from the non-optimized code.

This is the root of the problem: other optimizations transform the code in ways that confuse the tracking in `OptStackOps`. The `if` statement gets optimized to `lda _b; beq L0003`, and the label is moved, causing the tracking to associate `lda _b` with the LHS instead of `lda _c`.

Let me think about this differently. The bug is caused by the `if` statement's label confusing the tracking. The `if` creates a code path that:
1. Loads `b`
2. Checks if `b != 0`
3. If true, executes `b = 0`
4. Then loads `c` and does the subtraction

The optimizer sees that `b` is always 0, so the `if` is always false. It optimizes away the `if` body and the condition check, but the label remains (or gets moved). This causes the tracking to incorrectly associate `lda _b` as the LHS.

The real fix should be to ensure the tracking correctly handles this case. But that's a complex fix.

```c
    /* Rhs load entries may be removed */
    D->Rhs.X.Flags |= LI_REMOVE;
}
```

If `Rhs.X` has no load entry (`LoadIndex < 0`), then `D->Rhs.X.ChgEntry` might be invalid. Actually, looking at line 1144:
```c
X = NewCodeEntry (OP65_LDX, AM65_IMM, MakeHexArg (0), 0, D->Rhs.X.ChgEntry->LI);
```

It dereferences `D->Rhs.X.ChgEntry`. If `Rhs.X` has no load, `ChgEntry` might be set from `ChgIndex` which could be anything (including -1). Let me check `FinalizeLoadRegInfo`:
```c
if (LRI->ChgIndex >= 0) {
    LRI->ChgEntry = CS_GetEntry (S, LRI->ChgIndex);
} else {
    LRI->ChgEntry = 0;
}
```

If `ChgIndex < 0`, `ChgEntry` is 0 (NULL). So dereferencing it would crash!

But the debug shows `Rhs.X.ChgIdx=5` (not -1), so `ChgEntry` would be set. But `LoadEntry` is NULL (LoadIdx=-1).

In `Opt_a_tosbitwise` line 1144, if `OPC == OP65_EOR` and `Rhs.X.LoadEntry` is NULL but `ChgEntry` is not, it might work (using ChgEntry for line info). But if `Rhs.X` has no flags at all (like in our bug case), the code might still work because it just sets `LI_REMOVE` or `LI_DONT_REMOVE` on flags that are 0.

OK, I'm going down a rabbit hole. Let me just focus on the minimal fix.

The PR wants the CHECK failure to be resolved. The CHECK is:
```c
CHECK ((D->Rhs.A.Flags & D->Rhs.X.Flags & LI_DIRECT) != 0);
```

This requires both A and X to have LI_DIRECT. But `Opt_a_tossub` only needs A to have LI_DIRECT (it only calls `AddOpLow` with `&D->Rhs`, which only uses A). The X part is handled by sign extension.

So the CHECK is overly strict. Changing it to only check A is correct.

But the bug case reveals that when X has no flags at all, the tracking might be unreliable. However, this is a separate bug in the tracking, not in `Opt_a_tossub`.

Let me check if there are any existing tests that might break with my change. Let me run the test suite:

# ---- Display info during parsing phase ----
SILENT:=$(findstring s,$(word 1, $(MAKEFLAGS)))
ifneq ($(SILENT),s)
    $(info Using Makefile: $(realpath $(firstword $(MAKEFILE_LIST))) $(MAKECMDGOALS))
endif

# Makefile for the regression tests that return an error code on failure

ifneq ($(shell echo),)
  CMD_EXE = 1
endif

ifdef CMD_EXE
  S = $(subst /,\,/)
  NULLDEV = nul:
  MKDIR = mkdir $(subst /,\,$1)
  RMDIR = -rmdir /s /q $(subst /,\,$1)
  CATRES =
else
  S = /
  NULLDEV = /dev/null
  MKDIR = mkdir -p $1
  RMDIR = $(RM) -r $1
  CATRES = > $(WORKDIR)/$$@.out 2> $(WORKDIR)/$$@.out || (cat $(WORKDIR)/$$@.out && false)
endif

ifeq ($(SILENT),s)
    QUIET = 1
endif

ifdef QUIET
  .SILENT:
  NULLOUT = >$(NULLDEV)
  NULLERR = 2>$(NULLDEV)
ifndef CMD_EXE
  CATERR = 2> $(WORKDIR)/$$@.errlog || (cat $(WORKDIR)/$$@.errlog && false)
endif
endif

SIM65FLAGS = -x 4000000000 -c

CC65 := $(if $(wildcard ../../bin/cc65*),..$S..$Sbin$Scc65,cc65)
CA65 := $(if $(wildcard ../../bin/ca65*),..$S..$Sbin$Sca65,ca65)
LD65 := $(if $(wildcard ../../bin/ld65*),..$S..$Sbin$Sld65,ld65)
SIM65 := $(if $(wildcard ../../bin/sim65*),..$S..$Sbin$Ssim65,sim65)

WORKDIR = ../../testwrk/val

OPTIONS = g O Os Osi Osir Osr Oi Oir Or

.PHONY: all clean

SOURCES := $(wildcard *.c)
TESTS  = $(foreach option,$(OPTIONS),$(SOURCES:%.c=$(WORKDIR)/%.$(option).6502.prg))
TESTS += $(foreach option,$(OPTIONS),$(SOURCES:%.c=$(WORKDIR)/%.$(option).65c02.prg))

all: $(TESTS)

$(WORKDIR):
	$(call MKDIR,$(WORKDIR))

define PRG_template

$(WORKDIR)/%.$1.$2.prg: %.c | $(WORKDIR)
	$(if $(QUIET),echo val/$$*.$1.$2.prg)
	$(CC65) -t sim$2 $$(CC65FLAGS) --add-source -$1 -o $$(@:.prg=.s) $$< $(NULLOUT) $(CATERR)
	$(CA65) -t sim$2 -o $$(@:.prg=.o) $$(@:.prg=.s) $(NULLOUT) $(CATERR)
	$(LD65) -t sim$2 -o $$@ $$(@:.prg=.o) sim$2.lib $(NULLOUT) $(CATERR)
	$(SIM65) $(SIM65FLAGS) $$@ $(CATRES)

endef # PRG_template

$(foreach option,$(OPTIONS),$(eval $(call PRG_template,$(option),6502)))
$(foreach option,$(OPTIONS),$(eval $(call PRG_template,$(option),65c02)))

clean:
	@$(call RMDIR,$(WORKDIR))
