Let me think about this more carefully.

The PR description says the CHECK fails. My fix changes the CHECK to only check A (which is what the function actually needs). This prevents the crash.

The incorrect code generation in the specific test case is caused by a different issue (the tracking incorrectly identifies the LHS load when there's a label from an `if` statement). This is a pre-existing bug that was masked by the CHECK crash.

But wait, I should verify: does the incorrect code generation happen ONLY with my fix, or would it also happen if the original CHECK passed (i.e., if both A and X had LI_DIRECT)?

In the bug case, X doesn't have LI_DIRECT (or any flags). So the original CHECK would fail, and the optimization would not be applied. The code would fall back to the non-optimized version (which works correctly). So the original CHECK, while overly strict for correct cases, was preventing this buggy case from proceeding.

If I change the CHECK to only check A, the buggy case proceeds and generates wrong code.

So maybe I should NOT change the CHECK, but instead fix the precondition to reject this case. The precondition `RegAPreCondOk` should check that both A and X have the required flags when `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` is set, just like `PreCondOk` does for non-RegA functions.

But wait, the RegA functions (`Opt_a_tosand`, `Opt_a_tosor`, `Opt_a_tosxor`) don't need X to be direct. They only use `Rhs.A` via `AddOpLow`. If we change the precondition to require X to be direct, these functions would be rejected even when they could work correctly.

However, looking at `Opt_a_tosbitwise`, it uses `D->Rhs.X.ChgEntry` at line 1144, which requires `Rhs.X` to have a valid `ChgEntry`. If `Rhs.X` has no flags (like in the bug case), `ChgEntry` might be valid (if `ChgIndex >= 0`) or NULL (if `ChgIndex < 0`).

In the bug case, `Rhs.X.ChgIdx=5` (valid), so `ChgEntry` would be non-NULL. But `LoadEntry` is NULL (LoadIdx=-1). So the code at line 1144 would work (it only uses `ChgEntry` for line info).

But `Opt_a_tossub` doesn't use `Rhs.X` at all! It only uses `AddOpLow` with `&D->Rhs`, which only accesses `Rhs.A`. So `Opt_a_tossub` should work correctly even if `Rhs.X` has no flags.

The incorrect code generation is not because `Opt_a_tossub` uses `Rhs.X` incorrectly. It's because the LHS tracking is wrong (the LHS is associated with `lda _b` instead of `lda _c`).

So the fix should be in the tracking, not in the CHECK. But fixing the tracking is complex.

Given the time, let me consider a simpler approach: revert the CHECK change and instead modify `RegAPreCondOk` to check both A and X for `OP_RHS_LOAD` and `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` (like `PreCondOk` does). This would make the precondition fail for the bug case, and the optimization would not be applied. The code would fall back to calling `tossubax` (which works correctly).

But this would also affect `Opt_a_tosand`, `Opt_a_tosor`, `Opt_a_tosxor` which have the same flags. Let me check if those functions can handle X without LI_DIRECT:

`Opt_a_tosbitwise`:
- If `Rhs.A` is LI_DIRECT: uses `Rhs.A.LoadEntry->AM` and `Rhs.A.LoadEntry->Arg`
- If `Rhs.A` is not LI_DIRECT: tries to use Lhs.A or ZP
- For X: if X is used after the op, it either replaces with 0 (for EOR) or marks as don't-remove. If X is not used, it marks for removal.

If `Rhs.X` has no load instruction, `D->Rhs.X.ChgEntry` is used for line info (at line 1144). If `ChgIndex >= 0`, it's fine. If `ChgIndex < 0`, it would be NULL and crash.

But in our bug case, `ChgIndex=5` which is valid. So `Opt_a_tosbitwise` would not crash.

However, if we change the precondition to require both A and X to have `LI_DIRECT`, these functions would be rejected when X doesn't have `LI_DIRECT`, even though they could handle it. This might cause performance regressions (missed optimization opportunities) but not correctness issues.

I think the safest approach for now is:
1. Keep my CHECK change (only check A)
2. Also modify `RegAPreCondOk` to check both A and X for `OP_RHS_LOAD` and `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`, matching the behavior of `PreCondOk`

But wait, that would still allow the bug case because the precondition would fail and the optimization wouldn't be applied. The code would work correctly (fallback to non-optimized version).

Actually, let me reconsider. Maybe I should just revert my CHECK change and instead change the precondition. That way, the original CHECK stays (as a safety net), and the precondition prevents the bug case from reaching it.

Let me look at what `RegAPreCondOk` checks for RHS:

```c
if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD) != 0) {
    if ((RhsLo->Flags & LI_LOAD_INSN) == 0) {
        /* Cannot optimize */
        break;
    } else if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT) != 0) {
        if ((RhsLo->Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0) {
            /* Cannot optimize */
            break;
        }
    }
}
```

I can change it to:
```c
if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD) != 0) {
    if ((RhsLo->Flags & RhsHi->Flags & LI_LOAD_INSN) == 0) {
        /* Cannot optimize */
        break;
    } else if ((Desc->Flags & OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT) != 0) {
        if ((RhsLo->Flags & RhsHi->Flags & LI_DIRECT) == 0) {
            /* Cannot optimize */
            break;
        }
    }
}
```

This would make `RegAPreCondOk` consistent with `PreCondOk`. But it might reject some valid optimizations.

Actually, wait. The comment in `RegAPreCondOk` says:
```c
/* Currently we have only LHS/RHS checks with identical requirements for A/X,
** so we don't need to check twice for now.
*/
```

This means they assume that if A has a flag, X also has it. But the bug case shows this assumption is wrong: A has `LI_LOAD_INSN` but X doesn't.

So the fix should be to remove this assumption and check both A and X. Let me do that.

But I also need to check what happens with `Opt_a_tosbitwise` when X doesn't have `LI_LOAD_INSN`. If we add the check, those functions would not be called in such cases. But are there cases where they are currently called with X not having `LI_LOAD_INSN`? Let me check the debug output from the simple test (without `if`):

```

Lhs.X Flags=10001 LoadIdx=0 ChgIdx=0
Rhs.A Flags=10001 LoadIdx=3 ChgIdx=3
Rhs.X Flags=10001 LoadIdx=0 ChgIdx=0
```

Here, Lhs.X has `LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_DIRECT` (0x10001). But wait, `LoadIdx=0` for Lhs.X and `LoadIdx=0` for Rhs.X - they share the same load! That's because the `ldx #$00` before `lda _c` is used for both LHS and RHS (since both have X=0).

So in this correct case, both A and X have `LI_LOAD_INSN`. The bug case is the anomaly where X has no load.

I think changing the precondition to check both A and X is the right approach. But let me also revert my CHECK change and see if the combination works.

Actually, let me take a step back. The simplest fix that addresses the PR is:
1. Change the precondition `RegAPreCondOk` to check both A and X for `OP_RHS_LOAD` and `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`.

This prevents `Opt_a_tossub` from being called in the bug case, so the CHECK is never reached. The optimization falls back to the non-optimized version, which works correctly.

Now let me also think about edge cases. My changes to `RegAPreCondOk`:

1. Added `LhsHi` and `RhsHi` variables and set them
2. Changed LHS/RHS load checks to require both A and X (like `PreCondOk`)
3. Changed LHS/RHS remove checks to also check Hi load entries

This makes `RegAPreCondOk` consistent with `PreCondOk`. Functions that use `OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` now require both A and X to have `LI_DIRECT`, which matches the CHECK in `Opt_a_tossub` (and other functions).

But wait, there are functions in `FuncRegATable` that have `OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT`:
- `tosandax` -> `Opt_a_tosand` -> `Opt_a_tosbitwise`
- `tosorax` -> `Opt_a_tosor` -> `Opt_a_tosbitwise`
- `tossubax` -> `Opt_a_tossub`
- `tosxorax` -> `Opt_a_tosxor` -> `Opt_a_tosbitwise`

For `Opt_a_tosbitwise`, the function only needs `Rhs.A` to be direct (it has fallback for when it's not). But with my change, it now also requires `Rhs.X` to be direct. This might prevent some valid optimizations.

However, looking at the debug output from the simple case (which is a typical case):
```
Lhs.A Flags=10011 LoadIdx=1 ChgIdx=1
Lhs.X Flags=10001 LoadIdx=0 ChgIdx=0
Rhs.A Flags=10001 LoadIdx=3 ChgIdx=3
Rhs.X Flags=10001 LoadIdx=0 ChgIdx=0
```

Both A and X have `LI_LOAD_INSN | LI_DIRECT`. So typical cases should still work.

The only case where X doesn't have `LI_LOAD_INSN` is when the tracking is confused (like the bug case). So preventing optimization in those cases is actually the right thing to do, because the tracking is unreliable.

The functions with `OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT | OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` are:
- `tosandax` -> `Opt_a_tosand` -> `Opt_a_tosbitwise`
- `tosorax` -> `Opt_a_tosor` -> `Opt_a_tosbitwise`
- `tossubax` -> `Opt_a_tossub`
- `tosxorax` -> `Opt_a_tosxor` -> `Opt_a_tosbitwise`

All others have `OP_NONE`.

With my change, these four functions now require both RHS A and X to have `LI_LOAD_INSN` and `LI_DIRECT`. Previously, they only required A. This might cause some optimizations to not be applied when X doesn't have these flags.

But as I discussed, the case where X doesn't have these flags while A does is likely a tracking anomaly (like the bug case). In normal code, both A and X should have loads before `pushax`. So this change should be safe.

2026-05-29 02:12:58,053 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
All bitwise operations work correctly.

Now I'm confident that my fix is correct. Let me summarize the changes:

## Summary

The bug was that `Opt_a_tossub` (and potentially other RegA-only optimization functions) had a CHECK that required both `Rhs.A` and `Rhs.X` to have `LI_DIRECT` flag set, but the precondition check `RegAPreCondOk` only verified this for `Rhs.A` (not `Rhs.X`). When the X register didn't have `LI_DIRECT` (due to tracking issues with labels created by `if` statements), the CHECK would fail and crash the compiler.

The fix modifies `RegAPreCondOk` to check both A and X registers for LHS/RHS load and remove preconditions, making it consistent with `PreCondOk` (the non-RegA precondition check). This prevents the optimization from being applied when the tracking information is unreliable, avoiding both the crash and potential incorrect code generation.

Specifically:
1. Added `LhsHi` and `RhsHi` variables to `RegAPreCondOk`
2. Changed `OP_LHS_LOAD`/`OP_LHS_LOAD_DIRECT` checks to require both A and X (like `PreCondOk`)
3. Changed `OP_RHS_LOAD`/`OP_RHS_LOAD_DIRECT` checks to require both A and X (like `PreCondOk`)
4. Changed `OP_LHS_REMOVE`/`OP_LHS_REMOVE_DIRECT` checks to also check Hi load entries (like `PreCondOk`)
5. Changed `OP_RHS_REMOVE`/`OP_RHS_REMOVE_DIRECT` checks to also check Hi load entries (like `PreCondOk`)

Let me do a final verification of the PR test case:











🎬 ACTION
